<div id="review_238853883" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238853883" />
    <a title="Jianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4712378-jianne"><img alt="Jianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458899539p2/4712378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238853883?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jianne" href="/user/show/4712378-jianne">Jianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4712378-jianne?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238853883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6825098852392691622"><i>The Dead and the Gone</i> has not made it up to my expectations especially after <b>loving</b> <i>Life As We Knew It</i>. I'll talk more about the problems that I found in the book rather than the ones I liked (which were fewer actually)<br/><br/>Alex Morales is a seventeen-year-old Puerto Rican New Yorker whose parents disappear in the aftermath of the tidal waves, must must now care for his two younger sisters, Julie and Brianna even when hope seems all gone.<br/><br/>The novel explores on how a young man takes on unimaginable res</span>
  <span id="freeText6825098852392691622" style="display:none"><i>The Dead and the Gone</i> has not made it up to my expectations especially after <b>loving</b> <i>Life As We Knew It</i>. I'll talk more about the problems that I found in the book rather than the ones I liked (which were fewer actually)<br><br>Alex Morales is a seventeen-year-old Puerto Rican New Yorker whose parents disappear in the aftermath of the tidal waves, must must now care for his two younger sisters, Julie and Brianna even when hope seems all gone.<br><br>The novel explores on how a young man takes on unimaginable responsibilities. Do I agree with that? <i>Yes and No</i>. Well, first of all Alex is not really going to be your ideal elder brother, I'm sorry but that's what I think. Why? The most important of them all of that <b>he doesn't treat his sister equally</b>. He prefers Brianna over Julie, though I understand why. Julie really is annoying. But c'mon, it's nearly the end of the world and he still has to choose favorites. I just feel that if he had to choose whom to save of course he'd prefer one over the other, right? And it's just really pissing me off. Being the eldest can be such a responsibility in times like this especially but show your sisters that can look up to you and really trust that you won't let anything happen to them. But that's not what I see. I have an elder brother too though I'm the middle child and the only girl, my brother treats me and my younger brother equally so not complaints.<br><br>Another factor is that the love-hate relationship between Alex and Julie. First he'll shout at her then he'll say sorry, then he'll hurt her then say sorry then she'll get mad at him then she'll say she's sorry and the cycle goes on you know. And it's just really annoying because I know in times like this you really feel like you're going to give up and two sisters depending on you true but like a said, a responsible brother would know how to act besides they're all in this together, that's why he has a sister all his burden he can share it with them he doesn't have to carry it alone now will he?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380344055ra/699144.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just feel that there is really no hope in this book, it's more devastating and desperate than the first book. And that idea of body shopping, I don't think that in that actual situation that's really gonna happen, people are desperate for food they won't just give it away. Money is not a problem here anymore. It's just food, shelter, medicine and survival.<br><br>I just really can't connect with the characters. At all. The beginning is fine then it just dropped because of the characters not the plot entirely. Brianna's annoying, Julie's annoying and Alex's annoying. And all the other characters as well. Nothing really much to like about now is there?<br><br>And I don't like the third person narrative here, I guess it would've been easier to connect with Alex's character if it was first person narrative. And Julie and Brianna's name doesn't match with the Alex, Luis, Carlos and Isabelle's name which seems more Puerto Rican.<br><br>Alex, Luis and Carlos. Wow. Reminds me of the Funetes brothers much, from <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> well, I realized how much I miss them!<br><br>Anyway, <i>The Dead and the Gone</i> really is dead. There's almost no happy moments really. It's too depressing and despair is all in the book. Three stars really because it's not really that bad, depressing and all I can take that, the plot's fine it's really just the characters really.<br><br>And comparing it to other books that I've rated three stars, they're pretty much on the same track.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6825098852392691622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1362052494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362052494" />
    <a title="Josie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21250-josie"><img alt="Josie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344784207p2/21250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362052494?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josie" href="/user/show/21250-josie">Josie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780547422268" href="/book/show/8203319-the-dead-and-the-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21250-josie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21250-josie?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362052494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4112047028860371909">Ugh, this should have been a DNF, but I didn't want to skip this and go onto #3 in the series just in case there was some context I missed out on, or characters from this book that show up later. But god, it was awful. The third person POV just didn't work -- there was literally NO EMOTION the whole way through -- and the storyline (asteroid hits the moon, world thrown into chaos) was pretty much identical to <i>Life As We Knew It</i>. What was the point of going from the beginning again? As a reader, </span>
  <span id="freeText4112047028860371909" style="display:none">Ugh, this should have been a DNF, but I didn't want to skip this and go onto #3 in the series just in case there was some context I missed out on, or characters from this book that show up later. But god, it was awful. The third person POV just didn't work -- there was literally NO EMOTION the whole way through -- and the storyline (asteroid hits the moon, world thrown into chaos) was pretty much identical to <i>Life As We Knew It</i>. What was the point of going from the beginning again? As a reader, I already knew what was coming, but for some reason Alex was ridiculously uninformed. Random characters kept popping up to say things like "Have you heard about the tsunamis/volcanoes/epidemics/etc?" WHY YES, I BELIEVE I READ ABOUT THAT IN BOOK #1.<br /><br />Also, Alex is possibly THE MOST chauvinistic character I've come across. I kept thinking how much he didn't deserve to live. He thinks it's perfectly okay to hit his younger sisters, because he's the man of the house now! And that's how he's going to keep them in line!<br /><br />At one point Alex throws a paddy because his shirts are dirty. Yep, in a post-apocalyptic world he worries about looking nice. So he whines to Julie that she should do a better job washing them (without electricity, and oh by the way she is TWELVE YEARS OLD) and when she says, um hey I have an idea <i>wash your own freaking shirts</i> he grabs her and threatens to withhold food from her. What a great brother!<br /><br />And later, when Julie is all "you do realise I do all the cooking and cleaning, right?" Alex's chivalrous response is "but I thought you liked cooking and cleaning, and how hard is it anyway?" UM DID YOU MISS THE BIT WHERE THERE IS NO ELECTRICITY? IT IS HARD, OKAY.<br /><br />There's a great line near the end when Alex thinks about "how often he'd felt burdened by his sisters." Oh, you mean the sisters who do your laundry, your cooking, and your cleaning -- those sisters? What a burden they've been! ARGHHHH.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4112047028860371909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24442110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24442110" />
    <a title="Dave S." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/687033-dave-s"><img alt="Dave S." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24442110?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dave S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave S." href="/user/show/687033-dave-s">Dave S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people with twisted minds who like sad endings and corpses.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer24442110&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24442110" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15104739714297896870">Life as we Knew It was an amazing novel, and this was <s>an amazing</s> a terrible completely got that me convinced that Susan Beth Pfeffer was <s>an amazing author</s> a terrible author, At first, Pfeffer paints a realistic and exquisite picture of a latino family, which slowly starts to tear apart after a near-apocalyptic disaster. At first, the book is completely believable, as are the characters, but slowly, the characters become far to unrealistic. Too religious, too understanding, too oblivious, etc. An</span>
  <span id="freeText15104739714297896870" style="display:none">Life as we Knew It was an amazing novel, and this was <s>an amazing</s> a terrible completely got that me convinced that Susan Beth Pfeffer was <s>an amazing author</s> a terrible author, At first, Pfeffer paints a realistic and exquisite picture of a latino family, which slowly starts to tear apart after a near-apocalyptic disaster. At first, the book is completely believable, as are the characters, but slowly, the characters become far to unrealistic. Too religious, too understanding, too oblivious, etc. And soon enough, it becomes near unreadable. Will the fifteen year old girl start acting her age and stop being called Brush? NO! Will Alex stop stealing from the dead even though he thinks it is sinful? No! Will Kevin stop reading Playboy? No! And (spoilers...) Will they all survive? NO! There. I just saved you from reading a terrible crapload of a book. And quite frankly, I don't care. As much as I tried to like this book, I just couldn't. And I later realized it was terrible.</span>

<div id="review_1415205288" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415205288" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/234533-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601257982p2/234533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1415205288?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/234533-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9478415-the-dead-and-the-gone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/234533-amber?shelf=the-end">the-end</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1415205288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17052934382752113546">This is the second book in the Last Survivor series and I wished that I had read the book descriptions beforehand a little more carefully because I would have skipped book 2 and read book 3 instead. This book deals with the same catastrophic event that the first book (Life As We Knew It) does, but it is told through the eyes of a teenage boy, Alex, in New York whereas the first book is about a teenage girl, Miranda, in Pennsylvania. The 2 books mirror each other in many ways. The third book cont</span>
  <span id="freeText17052934382752113546" style="display:none">This is the second book in the Last Survivor series and I wished that I had read the book descriptions beforehand a little more carefully because I would have skipped book 2 and read book 3 instead. This book deals with the same catastrophic event that the first book (Life As We Knew It) does, but it is told through the eyes of a teenage boy, Alex, in New York whereas the first book is about a teenage girl, Miranda, in Pennsylvania. The 2 books mirror each other in many ways. The third book continues on with Miranda’s story and that is the story that really interests me. The story of Alex and his family were entertaining, but the story wasn’t as engrossing as Miranda’s. So, I feel like I went on a little detour in this series and will read the third book because I want to catch up with Miranda and see how life turns out for her. Even though I felt for Alex and the hardships he had to face, I didn’t like his character much and I got tired of all the praying and spiritual interest he and his sisters had. Supposedly the 4th book brings Alex’s and Miranda’s story’s together, but I have heard that book isn’t very good. I guess I will see what I think after book 3 to see if I want to continue. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Side Note: One thing in the book that drove me crazy in this book was the use of elevators. With the power being so unreliable and almost never working, they would still use the elevators in their building when the power was on. Weren’t they ever afraid of getting trapped without food or water? Then Alex’s sister dies in this exact way in the elevator and they still continued to use it. How dumb can you be? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17052934382752113546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_9867814'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9867814-ashen-winter"><img alt="Ashen Winter (Ashfall, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1332342080l/9867814._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ltpUQpkZ/JE2FVNU+/G3vWdEsVXJo5xMk3K4H1ipXMzvXz/9Fm3UZwN/m3zzz5A+TgqFd9bNpbmoReP9TnCJUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bruZvNWskwYlDJf+HLudak1yhI1emuLz1iV2rNL1rDcXPvIDWti78BBmX9YUhbrpZDywr0H02wbtEi1OxCx5qA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<a href="/author/show/1318.Susan_Beth_Pfeffer"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1228492581p3/1318.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2746625183462666447">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't </span>
  <span id="freeText2746625183462666447" style="display:none">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't until 1970 that her first book, Just Morgan, was published. She wrote it during her last semester at New York University; since then, she has been a full-time writer for young people. <br /><br />She has won numerous awards and citations for her work, which range from picture books to middle-grade and young-adult novels, and include both contemporary and historical fiction. She is also the author of the popular Portraits of Little Women series for grades 3-6, and has written a book for adults on writing for children.<br /><br />To date, she has written more than 60 books. About David was awarded the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award. The Year Without Michael is an ALA Best Book for Young Adults and winner of the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award; it was also named by the American Library Association as one of the hundred best books for teenagers written between 1968-1993. <br /><br />When she is not working, she enjoys watching movies, both new and old, and collecting movie memorabilia, reading biographies and histories, and eating foods that are bad for her. She lives in Middletown, New York, with her two cats, Alexander and Emily.<br /><br />Named the American Library Associations Young Adult Library Services Association Best Book for Young Adults 2007 and Teens’ Top Ten Booklist in 2007. Finalist for the Andre Norton Award, Quill Awards, Hal Clement Awards</span>
  <a data-text-id="2746625183462666447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
